الربوبية عند الثنوية أحق أن يكون بنفسه منه عند المعتزلة، وفى ذلك إزالة القدرة الله أن يكون بذاته، وهو أقبح قول والثانى كذبهم، إذ ثبتوا للعيد في نوع فعله جميع ما ثبتوا للصانع، ولم يثبتوا له اسم الألوهية الذى عرف الله به من فعل الإنشاء، وكذلك اسم الخالق مع ما كانت المعتزلة يزيدون في رتبة قدرة العبد القادر على قدرة الله؛ لأنهم يقولون : إن الله لا يقدر بالموعود أن يكون، وبما كان الوفاء فعله، منع الوصف بالقدرة، وذلك نحو ما ضرب لعبيده مددا ولهم أرزاقا قدرها لهم، ثم يجيء عبد فيقتله قبل استيفائه مدته وانجازه وعده، على بقاء قدرته، والله تعالى لا يقدر على منع العبد مما هو فعله، يريد الوفاء به على غير منع القدرة عنه، فصارت قدرة العبد أعظم، ومشيئة أنفذ، جل ربنا وتعالى عن هذا الوصف .. والثنوية تزعم أن النور وقع فى حبس الظلمة ووثاقها ! من الوجه الذى هم به الصلاح ودفع شرها عن جوهره، وكذلك الظلمة على قول من يجعل ابتداء
Then from what Allah knows to be; the doctrine of the Mu'tazila is that the servant has power over an external act, since everyone whom Allah knows will be a disbeliever has the power to become a believer. In truth, that necessitated for the servant a power of concealing the act from [؟] and [؟]. So likewise if there were another god: this is for you to know that their doctrine in reality is the doctrine of the Zandaqa; because that by which tawhid is established is that which invalidates both doctrines. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And the second point: They affirm for the servant power in negating all his [the servant's] management from procreation and repelling His threat from His saying: 'I will fill Hell'. And they affirm the actions of all disbelievers and devils other than what Allah wills to be; rather He wills it not to be, and He expends all that is in His treasures to prevent that, such that if He wanted to add anything to it He would not be able. Then they did not prevent the statement of the deity, and the creation stood upon what is in His knowledge of its stability and existence, so likewise in the matter of the world. And it clarifies what I informed you: that their doctrine produces the doctrine of the Dahriyya and the Zandaqa, not the doctrine of the people of Islam. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And the doctrine of the Zandaqa is that the world was the act of two, neither of whom has any making, nor management, nor power over the act of the other, and that each one of them is unique to a type of action, from evil and good, which the other cannot do. And likewise is the doctrine of the Magians. And according to the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, the servant has power over a type of action, which is acquisition (kasb), and the Worshipped has a type, which is creation (ijad). And Allah has no power over what the servant has, nor any making, nor does the servant have over what Allah has. And upon these two matters the management of the world turns. So they disgraced themselves with what I mentioned in the conclusion. Then the doctrine of these became even more ugly in that they assigned Him power over what the servant has of stillness and motion. So when Allah gave the servant power over them, power departed from Him. And we do not see the dualists removing the power of one of them by enabling the other, so that the meaning of power in that to which lordship is attributed among the dualists is more worthy of being by itself than it is among the Mu'tazila. And in that is the removal of power from Allah that He should be by Himself, and it is the ugliest statement. And the second is their lie, for they affirmed for the servant in his type of action all that they affirmed for the Maker, yet they did not affirm for him the name of divinity by which Allah is known from the act of creation, nor the name of Creator, while the Mu'tazila used to increase the rank of the servant's power over that of Allah; because they say that Allah cannot bring about what is promised to be, and because the fulfillment was His act, they prevent the description of power. And that is like when He appointed for His servants terms and provisions which He determined for them, then a servant comes and kills him before the completion of his term and the fulfillment of His promise, while his power remains; and Allah Almighty cannot prevent the servant from what is His act, He wills to fulfill it without prevention of power from it. Thus the servant's power became greater, and his will more penetrating. Exalted is our Lord and High above this description. And the dualists claim that light fell into the prison of darkness and its fetters, from the aspect by which they are for good and the repelling of its evil from its essence, and likewise darkness according to the one who makes the beginning...
Source pages p. 689

Commentary
This passage is a sustained refutation of the Mu'tazila, accusing them of falling into a form of dualism (thanawiyya) and Zandaqa (atheism). Maturidi begins by stating that the Mu'tazila attribute to the servant (al-'abd) an independent power to perform an external act, such that even a person predestined to be a disbeliever could choose belief. This grants the servant a power of concealment and independent action, which logically would imply the existence of another god. Thus their doctrine is essentially that of the Zandaqa (heretics), because the very principle that establishes tawhid is what negates both their view and dualism. The 'second point' (al-harf al-thani) further criticizes the Mu'tazila for affirming that the servant has power to negate divine decrees (e.g., procreation, God's threat to fill Hell) and to perform acts of disbelievers and devils contrary to God's will. They claim God tries to prevent but cannot, yet they still affirm a god. This leads to the conclusion that their doctrine is identical to that of the Dahriyya (materialists) and Zandaqa, not Islam. Maturidi then contrasts the Zandaqa and Magian dualisms—where each of two agents is independent and powerless over the other's acts—with the Mu'tazila view that the servant has kasb (acquisition) and God has ijad (creation). This divides the governance of the world between two independent sources, which is essentially dualism. He then highlights a further absurdity: when God grants the servant power over motion and stillness, God's own power over those actions ceases, which is worse than dualism since the dualists do not remove power from one deity when enabling the other. The Mu'tazila, by ascribing to the servant all the actions of the Creator (except the name 'God'), actually exalt the servant's power above God's, as they claim God cannot prevent a servant from killing someone before their appointed time, while the servant can. Therefore, the servant's power and will are greater than God's—a blasphemy. Finally, Maturidi mentions the dualist view of light trapped in darkness, highlighting how their conception of power is more coherent than that of the Mu'tazila.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila view is distinct from polytheism.
Correction: Maturidi shows it is essentially dualistic and even worse because it exalts human power over God.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, how does the Mu'tazila view compare with dualism?
A) It is more coherent
B) It is even more absurd because God loses power
C) It is exactly the same
D) It avoids dualism

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila division of power between God and man leads to a dualism that ultimately denies God's omnipotence and exalts human power above the divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a decision, do you truly believe that your power to act is utterly dependent on God's will, or do you sometimes feel as though your choices are completely your own? How would your reliance on God change if you fully internalized that your power is not independent but given and could be taken away at any moment?
?
Have you ever experienced a moment when your plans were overturned by circumstances beyond your control? Did that reveal a hidden assumption that your will should prevail? How does Maturidi's critique of the Mu'tazila challenge you to surrender the illusion of ultimate control?
?
If God's power can be 'removed' by giving it to you, as Maturidi says of the Mu'tazila view, then your very existence is a constant gift. Are you living with that awareness, or do you act as if your own power is self-sufficient? What one concrete change can you make today to acknowledge that your every action is only by His power?

Mu'tazila Doctrine Leads to Dualism
Maturidi compares Mu'tazila and dualist doctrines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that the Mu'tazila division of power between God and servant logically parallels dualist doctrines.

Core Idea
Dividing power between God and servant leads to dualism.

Maturidi begins by stating that what is in God's knowledge is its standing and being, and similarly for the world. He then clarifies that the Mu'tazila doctrine produces the doctrine of the Dahriyya and Zanadiqa, not Islam. In this passage, he outlines the dualist view and shows its similarity to the Mu'tazila view of two types of power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand Maturidi's comparison.
Notice how he starts with a general statement about knowledge.
2
Identify the two doctrines
Locate the description of dualist doctrine (Zanadiqa/Majus) and the Mu'tazila doctrine. Note their common structure: two independent agents with exclusive domains.
Dualists: two creators, one for good, one for evil. Mu'tazila: God has ijad, servant has kasb.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Maturidi says this leads away from Islam. Ask yourself why a strict separation of powers might be problematic for monotheism.
Hint: True tawhid requires God's power over all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما في علمه قيامه وكونه، فكذلك في أمر العالم. وهو يوضح ما أخبرتك أن مذهبهم ينتج مذهب أهل الدهر والزنادقة لا مذهب أهل الإسلام، والله الموفق. ومذهب الزنادقة أن العالم كان فعل اثنين ليس لأحدهما في فعل الآخر صنع ولا تدبير ولا قدرة، وأن كل واحد منهما ينفرد بنوع من الفعل من الشر والخير لا يقدر عليه الآخر. وكذلك مذهب المجوس. وعلى مذهب الاعتزال أن العبد له قدرة على نوع من الفعل وهو الكسب، وللمعبود نوع وهو الإيجاد، وليس لله على ما للعبد قدرة ولا صنع، ولا للعبد على ما لله قدرة ولا صنع، وعلى هذين الأمرين دار تدبير العالم، فضهوا به من ذكرت في التحصيل. ثم ازداد مذهب هؤلاء قبحا من حيث جعلوا منه قدرة على ما العبد من السكون والحركة، فلما أقدر الله العبد عليها ذهبت عنه القدرة، ولا نرى الثنوية تزيل قدرة واحد منهما بالتمكين من الآخر، ليعلم معنى القدرة في الذي أضيف إليه الربوبية عند الثنوية أحق أن يكون بنفسه منه عند المعتزلة، وفي ذلك إزالة القدرة عن الله أن يكون بذاته، وهو أقبح قول. والثاني كذبهم، إذ ثبتوا للعبد في نوع فعله جميع ما ثبتوا للصانع، ولم يثبتوا له اسم الألوهية الذي عرف الله به من فعل الإنشاء، وكذلك اسم الخالق مع ما كانت المعتزلة يزيدون في رتبة قدرة العبد القادر على قدرة الله؛ لأنهم يقولون: إن الله لا يقدر على الموعود أن يكون، وبما كان الوفاء فعله، منع الوصف بالقدرة، وذلك نحو ما ضرب لعبيده مددا ولهم أرزاقا قدرها لهم، ثم يجيء عبد فيقتله قبل استيفائه مدته وإنجازه وعده، على بقاء قدرته، والله تعالى لا يقدر على منع العبد مما هو فعله، يريد الوفاء به على غير منع القدرة عنه، فصارت قدرة العبد أعظم، ومشيئة أنفذ، جل ربنا وتعالى عن هذا الوصف.
What is in His knowledge is its standing and its being, so likewise in the matter of the world. And He clarifies what I informed you that their doctrine yields the doctrine of the Dahriyya and the Zanadiqa, not the doctrine of Islam, and God is the guide. The doctrine of the Zanadiqa is that the world was the act of two, neither of which has any making, management, or power in the act of the other, and that each of them is unique in a type of act, of evil and good, which the other cannot do. Likewise the doctrine of the Majus. According to the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, the servant has power over a type of act, which is acquisition (kasb), and the worshipped has a type, which is bringing into existence (ijad), and God has no power or making over what the servant has, nor does the servant have any over what God has, and upon these two matters the management of the world revolves. Thus they deviated with it from what I mentioned in al-Tahsil. Then the doctrine of these people increased in ugliness in that they made the power that the servant has over motion and rest come from Him, and when God empowered the servant over them, power left him, and we do not see the Dualists removing the power of either of them by enabling the other, so that the meaning of power in that to which lordship is attributed by the Dualists is more worthy of being by itself than it is in the case of the Mu'tazila, and in that is removal of power from God that He is by essence, and it is the ugliest statement. The second is their falsehood, for they affirmed for the servant in the type of his action all that they affirmed for the Maker, but they did not affirm for him the name of divinity by which God is known from the act of creation, and likewise the name of Creator, even though the Mu'tazila increase the rank of the power of the capable servant over God's power; because they say: God neither has power over the promised to be, and because fulfillment was His act, He is prevented from the description of power. That is like what He appointed for His servants terms and provisions which He determined for them, then a servant comes and kills him before the completion of his term and the fulfillment of His promise, while his power remains, and God Almighty does not have power to prevent the servant from what is His act—He intends to fulfill it without prevention of power from it. Thus the servant's power became greater and his will more penetrating. Glorious and exalted is our Lord above this description.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the Mu'tazila position on divine and human power, arguing that it leads to dualistic and Zoroastrian conclusions. Imam Maturidi begins by stating that what is in God's knowledge is its standing and being, and similarly for the world. He clarifies that the Mu'tazila doctrine yields the doctrine of the Dahriyya (materialists) and Zanadiqa (heretics), not Islam. He then describes the dualist view that the world is the act of two independent agents, each unique in its type of act. Similarly, the Mu'tazila hold that the servant has power over acquisition (kasb) and God over bringing into existence (ijad), with no overlap. This, Maturidi says, leads to the management of the world being based on two separate powers, which is a deviation. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for making the servant's power over motion and rest come from God, and then when God empowers the servant, that power leaves God, whereas the Dualists do not remove power from either agent. Thus the Mu'tazila's attributed power to the servant more appropriately belongs to God by essence. Maturidi calls this the ugliest statement. He then presents a second criticism: the Mu'tazila affirm for the servant in his type of action all that they affirm for the Maker (power to act), but they do not affirm for him the name of divinity or creator. Furthermore, they increase the rank of the servant's power over God's power by claiming that God cannot prevent the servant from violating His decree. For example, God sets terms and provisions for people, but a servant can kill someone before the term ends, and God cannot prevent it because the killing is the servant's act. Thus the servant's power is greater and his will more penetrating. Maturidi ends by exalting God above such descriptions.

المجوس
الكسب
الإيجاد
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazila and dualists are completely different theological systems.
Correction: Maturidi shows their logical structure is identical: two independent powers with exclusive domains.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Mu'tazila doctrine ultimately yield?
A) The doctrine of Islam
B) The doctrine of the Dahriyya and Zanadiqa
C) The doctrine of the Ash'ariyya
D) The doctrine of the Sufis

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that the Mu'tazila separation of power between God and servant mirrors dualist belief in two creators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of my life do I subconsciously act as if I have sole control, forgetting that God is the ultimate creator of every outcome? How can I actively acknowledge His sovereignty in those areas today?
?
When I attribute a success entirely to my own effort, am I unwittingly embracing a dualistic mindset? What would it look like to attribute every good deed to God's grace alone?
?
Do I ever resent God's decree as if it were an interference with my 'free will'? How does Maturidi's warning about dualism expose such resentment as a subtle form of shirk?

7 min
Mu'tazila View of Power and Its Contradiction
Maturidi criticizes Mu'tazila for removing power from God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's criticism that the Mu'tazila effectively remove power from God by making servant's power come from Him and then leave Him.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila view of power strips God of His essence.

In this second critique, Maturidi attacks the Mu'tazila claim that the servant's power over motion and rest comes from God, but when God empowers the servant, that power leaves God. He contrasts this with the dualists who do not remove power from either agent. Maturidi says this is an ugly statement that removes power from God as an essential attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the logic: God gives power, then power leaves God.
Notice the comparison with dualists who do not remove power.
2
Understand the logical problem
If God gives power to the servant over a type of act, and then that power no longer belongs to God, then God is not omnipotent over that type of act.
Dualists: each agent retains power over his own domain.
3
Reflect on the theological consequence
Maturidi says this means power in the sense of lordship (rububiyya) belongs more to the servant than to God, which is the ugliest statement.
This contradicts tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما في علمه قيامه وكونه، فكذلك في أمر العالم. وهو يوضح ما أخبرتك أن مذهبهم ينتج مذهب أهل الدهر والزنادقة لا مذهب أهل الإسلام، والله الموفق. ومذهب الزنادقة أن العالم كان فعل اثنين ليس لأحدهما في فعل الآخر صنع ولا تدبير ولا قدرة، وأن كل واحد منهما ينفرد بنوع من الفعل من الشر والخير لا يقدر عليه الآخر. وكذلك مذهب المجوس. وعلى مذهب الاعتزال أن العبد له قدرة على نوع من الفعل وهو الكسب، وللمعبود نوع وهو الإيجاد، وليس لله على ما للعبد قدرة ولا صنع، ولا للعبد على ما لله قدرة ولا صنع، وعلى هذين الأمرين دار تدبير العالم، فضهوا به من ذكرت في التحصيل. ثم ازداد مذهب هؤلاء قبحا من حيث جعلوا منه قدرة على ما العبد من السكون والحركة، فلما أقدر الله العبد عليها ذهبت عنه القدرة، ولا نرى الثنوية تزيل قدرة واحد منهما بالتمكين من الآخر، ليعلم معنى القدرة في الذي أضيف إليه الربوبية عند الثنوية أحق أن يكون بنفسه منه عند المعتزلة، وفي ذلك إزالة القدرة عن الله أن يكون بذاته، وهو أقبح قول. والثاني كذبهم، إذ ثبتوا للعبد في نوع فعله جميع ما ثبتوا للصانع، ولم يثبتوا له اسم الألوهية الذي عرف الله به من فعل الإنشاء، وكذلك اسم الخالق مع ما كانت المعتزلة يزيدون في رتبة قدرة العبد القادر على قدرة الله؛ لأنهم يقولون: إن الله لا يقدر على الموعود أن يكون، وبما كان الوفاء فعله، منع الوصف بالقدرة، وذلك نحو ما ضرب لعبيده مددا ولهم أرزاقا قدرها لهم، ثم يجيء عبد فيقتله قبل استيفائه مدته وإنجازه وعده، على بقاء قدرته، والله تعالى لا يقدر على منع العبد مما هو فعله، يريد الوفاء به على غير منع القدرة عنه، فصارت قدرة العبد أعظم، ومشيئة أنفذ، جل ربنا وتعالى عن هذا الوصف.

Misconception & Correction

What does Maturidi say about the dualists' view of power compared to the Mu'tazila?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when you succeed or act, do you subtly feel that the power came from you, not from God? How does this lesson accuse your heart of that hidden sin? Will you consciously attribute every movement and rest to God's power from now on?
?
Maturidi says that removing power from God is the ugliest statement. Have your thoughts or words ever effectively 'removed' power from God by relying on your own strength or abilities? When will you repent and return all power to its true Owner?
?
If you truly believed that God retains all power even while you act, how would your attitude towards your own accomplishments change? Would you be more humble, more grateful, and less anxious? What is stopping you from living that reality today?

Mu'tazila Affirm Servant's Power Over God's
Maturidi criticizes Mu'tazila for elevating servant's power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second critique: the Mu'tazila affirm for the servant all that they affirm for the Maker, yet deny him divinity, and even claim the servant's power exceeds God's in some respects.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila elevate servant's power above God's.

Maturidi presents a second criticism: the Mu'tazila affirm for the servant in his type of action all that they affirm for the Maker (power to act), but they do not affirm for him the name of divinity or creator. Furthermore, they increase the rank of the servant's power over God's power by claiming that God cannot prevent the servant from violating His decree. Maturidi gives the example of a servant killing someone before their term, while God cannot prevent it because the act belongs to the servant. Thus the servant's power is greater and his will more penetrating.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the structure: first part about affirming same attributes, second part about power comparison.
Notice the specific example of killing before term.
2
Analyze the first claim
The Mu'tazila give the servant all the attributes of the Maker (power to create actions) but refuse to call him divine or creator. Why is this inconsistent?
This shows they are reluctant to fully attribute divinity, but the logic of their position should lead to it.
3
Analyze the second claim
The Mu'tazila say God cannot prevent the servant from acting contrary to His decree. For example, a servant kills someone before their appointed term. God's promise of provision is thus thwarted. This implies the servant's power is greater.
Consider the implication: if God cannot prevent it, then the servant's will is more effective.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi ends by exalting God above this description. How does this critique reinforce the need for complete divine power?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما في علمه قيامه وكونه، فكذلك في أمر العالم. وهو يوضح ما أخبرتك أن مذهبهم ينتج مذهب أهل الدهر والزنادقة لا مذهب أهل الإسلام، والله الموفق. ومذهب الزنادقة أن العالم كان فعل اثنين ليس لأحدهما في فعل الآخر صنع ولا تدبير ولا قدرة، وأن كل واحد منهما ينفرد بنوع من الفعل من الشر والخير لا يقدر عليه الآخر. وكذلك مذهب المجوس. وعلى مذهب الاعتزال أن العبد له قدرة على نوع من الفعل وهو الكسب، وللمعبود نوع وهو الإيجاد، وليس لله على ما للعبد قدرة ولا صنع، ولا للعبد على ما لله قدرة ولا صنع، وعلى هذين الأمرين دار تدبير العالم، فضهوا به من ذكرت في التحصيل. ثم ازداد مذهب هؤلاء قبحا من حيث جعلوا منه قدرة على ما العبد من السكون والحركة، فلما أقدر الله العبد عليها ذهبت عنه القدرة، ولا نرى الثنوية تزيل قدرة واحد منهما بالتمكين من الآخر، ليعلم معنى القدرة في الذي أضيف إليه الربوبية عند الثنوية أحق أن يكون بنفسه منه عند المعتزلة، وفي ذلك إزالة القدرة عن الله أن يكون بذاته، وهو أقبح قول. والثاني كذبهم، إذ ثبتوا للعبد في نوع فعله جميع ما ثبتوا للصانع، ولم يثبتوا له اسم الألوهية الذي عرف الله به من فعل الإنشاء، وكذلك اسم الخالق مع ما كانت المعتزلة يزيدون في رتبة قدرة العبد القادر على قدرة الله؛ لأنهم يقولون: إن الله لا يقدر على الموعود أن يكون، وبما كان الوفاء فعله، منع الوصف بالقدرة، وذلك نحو ما ضرب لعبيده مددا ولهم أرزاقا قدرها لهم، ثم يجيء عبد فيقتله قبل استيفائه مدته وإنجازه وعده، على بقاء قدرته، والله تعالى لا يقدر على منع العبد مما هو فعله، يريد الوفاء به على غير منع القدرة عنه، فصارت قدرة العبد أعظم، ومشيئة أنفذ، جل ربنا وتعالى عن هذا الوصف.
What is in His knowledge is its standing and its being, so likewise in the matter of the world. And He clarifies what I informed you that their doctrine yields the doctrine of the Dahriyya and the Zanadiqa, not the doctrine of Islam, and God is the guide. The doctrine of the Zanadiqa is that the world was the act of two, neither of which has any making, management, or power in the act of the other, and that each of them is unique in a type of act, of evil and good, which the other cannot do. Likewise the doctrine of the Majus. According to the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, the servant has power over a type of act, which is acquisition (kasb), and the worshipped has a type, which is bringing into existence (ijad), and God has no power or making over what the servant has, nor does the servant have any over what God has, and upon these two matters the management of the world revolves. Thus they deviated with it from what I mentioned in al-Tahsil. Then the doctrine of these people increased in ugliness in that they made the power that the servant has over motion and rest come from Him, and when God empowered the servant over them, power left him, and we do not see the Dualists removing the power of either of them by enabling the other, so that the meaning of power in that to which lordship is attributed by the Dualists is more worthy of being by itself than it is in the case of the Mu'tazila, and in that is removal of power from God that He is by essence, and it is the ugliest statement. The second is their falsehood, for they affirmed for the servant in the type of his action all that they affirmed for the Maker, but they did not affirm for him the name of divinity by which God is known from the act of creation, and likewise the name of Creator, even though the Mu'tazila increase the rank of the power of the capable servant over God's power; because they say: God neither has power over the promised to be, and because fulfillment was His act, He is prevented from the description of power. That is like what He appointed for His servants terms and provisions which He determined for them, then a servant comes and kills him before the completion of his term and the fulfillment of His promise, while his power remains, and God Almighty does not have power to prevent the servant from what is His act—He intends to fulfill it without prevention of power from it. Thus the servant's power became greater and his will more penetrating. Glorious and exalted is our Lord above this description.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the Mu'tazila position on divine and human power, arguing that it leads to dualistic and Zoroastrian conclusions. Imam Maturidi begins by stating that what is in God's knowledge is its standing and being, and similarly for the world. He clarifies that the Mu'tazila doctrine yields the doctrine of the Dahriyya (materialists) and Zanadiqa (heretics), not Islam. He then describes the dualist view that the world is the act of two independent agents, each unique in its type of act. Similarly, the Mu'tazila hold that the servant has power over acquisition (kasb) and God over bringing into existence (ijad), with no overlap. This, Maturidi says, leads to the management of the world being based on two separate powers, which is a deviation. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for making the servant's power over motion and rest come from God, and then when God empowers the servant, that power leaves God, whereas the Dualists do not remove power from either agent. Thus the Mu'tazila's attributed power to the servant more appropriately belongs to God by essence. Maturidi calls this the ugliest statement. He then presents a second criticism: the Mu'tazila affirm for the servant in his type of action all that they affirm for the Maker (power to act), but they do not affirm for him the name of divinity or creator. Furthermore, they increase the rank of the servant's power over God's power by claiming that God cannot prevent the servant from violating His decree. For example, God sets terms and provisions for people, but a servant can kill someone before the term ends, and God cannot prevent it because the killing is the servant's act. Thus the servant's power is greater and his will more penetrating. Maturidi ends by exalting God above such descriptions.

الألوهية
القدرة
الموعود
الوفاء

Misconception: Mu'tazila view maintains God's sovereignty.
Correction: Maturidi shows it leads to servant's power being greater than God's, contradicting divine omnipotence.

B) A servant killing someone before their appointed term
C) A servant creating a mountain
D) A servant decreeing rain

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that the Mu'tazila position logically implies the servant's power surpasses God's, which is a grave error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make plans, do you truly believe that God's will overrides your own, or do you act as if your power to achieve them is independent of Him? What would change if you internalized that even your ability to act is subordinate to His power?
?
This passage shows that even a theological position aiming to defend justice can end up diminishing God's majesty. In your own life, are there ways you defend good principles (like fairness or responsibility) but at the cost of not fully relying on God's power? How can you correct that today?
?
Maturidi exalts God above the description that His power is limited by His servants' actions. Do you ever unconsciously assume that your choices constrain God's ability to work in your life? Confess one area where you need to repent of this and trust His power more.

Maturidi's Refutation of Dualism and Its Parallel with Mu'tazila
Maturidi refutes dualism and parallels it with Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes dualism by demonstrating it necessarily attributes error, ignorance, and incapacity to the divine light, and how he draws a parallel to certain Mu'tazila positions.

Core Idea
Dualism and Mu'tazilism both lead to attributing defect to the divine.

In this passage, Maturidi tackles a fundamental challenge to tawhid: the dualist claim that light and darkness are co-eternal principles. He shows that this view necessarily forces one to ascribe defect to the principle of light. He then draws a striking parallel with certain Mu'tazila positions, demonstrating that their own reasoning leads to similar contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the dualist claim
Start by reading the Arabic and translation of the dualist claim. Notice how they describe light falling into darkness for rectification.
2
Identify Maturidi's logical deduction
Maturidi states that the outcome contradicted the intention. Understand why this forces error, ignorance, and incapacity upon light.
Each attribute follows logically from the previous.
3
Examine the three attributes
Look at how Maturidi defines error (outcome not as intended), ignorance (lack of foreknowledge), and incapacity (inability to escape).
These are the three defects attributed to light.
4
Read the Mu'tazila parallel
Now read the Mu'tazila saying about God empowering creatures for obedience. Maturidi shows that if God's will is not achieved, the same defects apply.
5
Connect the critique
See how Maturidi concludes that the Mu'tazila statement 'resemblance to those I mentioned in all aspects of blame' — i.e., they fall into the same trap as dualists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثنوية تزعم أن النور وقع في حبس الظلمة ووثاقها من الوجه الذي هم به الصلاح ودفع شرها عن جوهره، وكذلك الظلمة على قول من يجعل ابتداء القدح منها، فأخطأ جميعا. الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي: خرج فعلها على خلاف ما أرادا، وصار كل واحد منهما في جهة من يد الآخر، فلزمهم القول في النور بالخطأ وبالجهل والعجز. أما الخطأ، فلما لم يكن عاقبته على ما أراد، والجهل؛ لما لم يكن علم أنه يبقى في وثاق عدوه، وأما العجز هو أنه في جهد الخلاص وتدبيره فلم يتهيأ له. وكذلك قول المعتزلة: إن الله لم يقو كافرا ولا أحدا إلا ليطيعه، ولا ملك أحدا شيئا إلا ليشكر، ولا خلق أحدا إلا ليخضع له، وكذلك يريد، وله فعل ما فعل، ولو كان منه غير هذا كان يكون سفيها ظالما، ثم لم يكن يجمع جميع ما أعطى أعداءه ما أراد، وله أخطاء، وذلك الخطأ المعروف أن لا يخرج الأمر على ما يريده، ثم القدرة على ما لم لو فعل لكان خارجا عن علمه، ثم ثبت من الفعل فيما بعد هو فعل الله في المنع منه، فأوجب قولهم مضاهاة من ذكرت بكل وجوه المذمة.
The Dualists claim that light fell into the prison of darkness and its bonds, from the aspect by which they intended rectification and repelling its evil from its essence, and likewise darkness according to the one who makes the beginning of defect from it, so they all erred. Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (said): their action came out contrary to what they both intended, and each of them became in a direction of the other's hand, so they are compelled to attribute error, ignorance, and incapacity to light. As for error, because its outcome was not as he intended; as for ignorance, because he did not know that he would remain in the bondage of his enemy; and as for incapacity, it is that he is in the effort of deliverance and his management, but it was not possible for him. Similarly the saying of the Mu'tazila: that God did not empower an unbeliever nor anyone except to obey Him, nor did He give anyone anything except to thank Him, nor did He create anyone except to submit to Him, and thus He wills, and He does what He does, and if it were other than this from Him, He would be foolish and unjust. Then all that He gave to His enemies did not achieve what He wanted, and He has errors, and that error is known that the matter does not come out as He intends. Then power over what if it were done would be outside His knowledge, then it is established from the act afterward that it is God's act in preventing it, so their statement necessitates resemblance to those I mentioned in all aspects of blame.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the dualist theory of light and darkness, followed by a comparison to the Mu'tazila. Maturidi begins by describing the dualist claim that light fell into the prison of darkness to rectify it and repel its evil, and darkness similarly originates defect. He declares that they all erred. He then states that their action resulted contrary to their intention, each becoming opposed to the other, forcing them to attribute error, ignorance, and incapacity to light. Error is proven because the outcome was not as intended; ignorance because light did not know it would remain in bondage; incapacity because light struggled for deliverance but could not achieve it. Maturidi then parallels this with the Mu'tazila saying: God only empowers and gives to creatures for obedience and gratitude, and if He did otherwise He would be foolish and unjust. Yet what He gave to His enemies did not achieve His desire, implying error in God. They claim God cannot prevent the servant's act because it is the servant's action, leading to the conclusion that God's will is frustrated. Thus, the Mu'tazila statement necessitates resemblance to the dualists in all aspects of blame.

الظلمة

الوثاق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism is a coherent alternative to monotheism.
Correction: Maturidi shows that dualism forces one to attribute error, ignorance, and incapacity to the divine light, which is incompatible with divinity.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that any system positing multiple ultimate principles or limiting God's power leads to theological absurdities, such as attributing error and incapacity to the divine.

?
Do you hold any belief, perhaps without realizing it, that suggests God is limited by human actions—such as thinking that our sins 'frustrate' His will? This lesson shows that even the Mu'tazila fell into that error. How will you realign your understanding to affirm God's absolute sovereignty and wisdom?
?
Consider a time you doubted God's wisdom because of a difficult outcome. In that moment, did you implicitly attribute some form of error or ignorance to Him? How can the truth that nothing escapes His will and knowledge, as taught in this lesson, transform how you process future hardships? What concrete step will you take to remind yourself of this?

Maturidi's Rejection of Denials of Creation and Divine Action
Maturidi rejects denials by Zanadiqa, Mushabbiha, and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the denials of the Zanadiqa (creation from nothing), Mushabbiha (anthropomorphism), and Mu'tazila (God's creation of actions).

Core Idea
Denying God's creative power leads to theological contradiction.

In this passage, Maturidi directly challenges three groups that undermine core Islamic beliefs about creation and divine omnipotence. The Zanadiqa reject creation ex nihilo, the Mushabbiha reduce God to a body, and the Mu'tazila deny that God creates human actions. Their errors stem from imposing limited human reasoning on the divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, notice the concise condemnation.
Pay attention to the formula 'Ankart...'
2
Identify the three groups and their denials
Find the Zanadiqa, Mushabbiha, and Mu'tazila and the specific claim Maturidi rejects for each.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Why does Maturidi consider these denials wrong? The commentary explains their reliance on limited human estimation.
4
Connect to tawheed
How do these denials affect the oneness and power of Allah?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وأنكرت الزنادقة قول شيء يحدث لا من شيء؛ ما لا يتصور مثله في الوهم، وكذلك المشبهة في قولهم بالجسم. وأنكرت المعتزلة خلق أفعال العباد؛ لما ليس بقائم في العقول ولا متوهم في الأوهام، وزعمت القدرية أن الله لا يدع الغاية من الخير الذي يقدر عليه إلا فعله. وكذلك قول الزنادقة أنه يفعل غاية الخير، وأن خالق الشر غيره. وكذلك قول القدرية أن الله لا يقدر على شيء موجود من الشر، وأنه كله فعل العباد. ويقول المعتزلة: إن الله لا يريد كون الشر لأحد أحد، ويريده الشيطان، ثم يكون ذلك وإن لم يكن ما يريده الله، كما قالت الزنادقة في كون ذلك من الشيطان، وخالق الشر وإن لم يرده الله.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: The Zanadiqa denied the statement that something comes into existence from nothing; that which cannot be imagined like it in estimation, and likewise the Mushabbiha in their statement of the body. The Mu'tazila denied the creation of the actions of servants, because it is not established in intellects nor imagined in estimations. The Qadariyya claimed that God does not leave the ultimate of good which He is able to do except He does it. Likewise the saying of the Zanadiqa that He does the ultimate good, and that the creator of evil is other than Him. Likewise the saying of the Qadariyya that God has no power over any existing evil, and that all of it is the act of servants. The Mu'tazila say that God does not will the occurrence of evil for anyone, and Satan wills it, then it occurs even though what God wills does not occur, just as the Zanadiqa said regarding its occurrence from Satan, and the creator of evil even if God does not will it.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is a categorical rejection of the theological denials made by different sects. Maturidi begins by stating that the Zanadiqa (heretics) denied creation from nothing, claiming it is unimaginable. Similarly, the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) affirmed a body for God. The Mu'tazila denied that God creates the actions of servants, arguing it is not rationally established. The Qadariyya claimed that God must always do the utmost good possible. Maturidi then shows parallels: the Zanadiqa say God does the ultimate good and that evil is created by another; the Qadariyya say God has no power over any existing evil and that all evil is the servant's act. The Mu'tazila say God does not will evil, but Satan wills it and it occurs even when God does not will it, similar to the Zanadiqa claim that evil comes from Satan as a separate creator. Thus, Maturidi exposes the shared errors of these sects in denying God's complete power and will over all things, including evil.

Key Terms
الزنادقة
المشبهة
المعتزلة
خلق أفعال العباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These sects are unrelated in their errors.
Correction: Maturidi groups them because they all rely on limited human reasoning to limit God's power.

Checkpoint
What do the Mu'tazila deny according to Maturidi?
A) Creation from nothing
B) God's body
C) Creation of actions of servants
D) God's will over evil

Key Takeaway
Maturidi exposes that denying God's creative power, whether through anthropomorphism or rationalism, contradicts tawheed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unconsciously limited God's power by thinking something is 'impossible' or 'unimaginable'—like the Zanadiqa did? What specific area of your life might you be trusting your own estimation over divine revelation? Commit now to surrender that to Allah this week.
?
The Mushabbiha reduced God to a body because they could not conceive of a reality beyond their senses. Where in your worship or understanding of Allah might you be falling into a subtle anthropomorphism (e.g., imagining Him with human emotions or actions in a literal way)? Write down one step you will take to purify your tawheed starting today.
?
The Mu'tazila denied that Allah creates your actions, placing full responsibility on you without divine involvement. Yet the truth is that every deed, good or bad, is under Allah's will. Does your daily life reflect this balance—relying on Allah for every action while taking responsibility? If not, what change can you make right now in your next prayer or task?

Maturidi's Rejection of Qadariyya and the Shared Error about Evil
Maturidi refutes Qadariyya and links their error to Zanadiqa and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the Qadariyya claim that God must do ultimate good and the shared error among Zanadiqa, Qadariyya, and Mu'tazila regarding evil and divine power.

Core Idea
Denying God's power over evil leads to polytheism or impotence.

Maturidi continues by exposing the Qadariyya's claim that God is obligated to do the utmost good. He then shows a striking parallel: the Zanadiqa say evil's creator is other than God, the Qadariyya say God has no power over evil, and the Mu'tazila say God does not will evil but Satan does. All three undermine God's absolute sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the chain of claims.
2
Identify the three sects' positions on evil
Find the positions of Zanadiqa, Qadariyya, and Mu'tazila regarding the origin and power over evil.
Use the key terms: الخير, الشر, الإرادة.
3
Recognize the common error
They all limit God's power or will over evil.
4
Understand Maturidi's implicit refutation
By listing them together, he shows their inconsistency with tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وأنكرت الزنادقة قول شيء يحدث لا من شيء؛ ما لا يتصور مثله في الوهم، وكذلك المشبهة في قولهم بالجسم. وأنكرت المعتزلة خلق أفعال العباد؛ لما ليس بقائم في العقول ولا متوهم في الأوهام، وزعمت القدرية أن الله لا يدع الغاية من الخير الذي يقدر عليه إلا فعله. وكذلك قول الزنادقة أنه يفعل غاية الخير، وأن خالق الشر غيره. وكذلك قول القدرية أن الله لا يقدر على شيء موجود من الشر، وأنه كله فعل العباد. ويقول المعتزلة: إن الله لا يريد كون الشر لأحد أحد، ويريده الشيطان، ثم يكون ذلك وإن لم يكن ما يريده الله، كما قالت الزنادقة في كون ذلك من الشيطان، وخالق الشر وإن لم يرده الله.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: The Zanadiqa denied the statement that something comes into existence from nothing; that which cannot be imagined like it in estimation, and likewise the Mushabbiha in their statement of the body. The Mu'tazila denied the creation of the actions of servants, because it is not established in intellects nor imagined in estimations. The Qadariyya claimed that God does not leave the ultimate of good which He is able to do except He does it. Likewise the saying of the Zanadiqa that He does the ultimate good, and that the creator of evil is other than Him. Likewise the saying of the Qadariyya that God has no power over any existing evil, and that all of it is the act of servants. The Mu'tazila say that God does not will the occurrence of evil for anyone, and Satan wills it, then it occurs even though what God wills does not occur, just as the Zanadiqa said regarding its occurrence from Satan, and the creator of evil even if God does not will it.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is a categorical rejection of the theological denials made by different sects. Maturidi begins by stating that the Zanadiqa (heretics) denied creation from nothing, claiming it is unimaginable. Similarly, the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) affirmed a body for God. The Mu'tazila denied that God creates the actions of servants, arguing it is not rationally established. The Qadariyya claimed that God must always do the utmost good possible. Maturidi then shows parallels: the Zanadiqa say God does the ultimate good and that evil is created by another; the Qadariyya say God has no power over any existing evil and that all evil is the servant's act. The Mu'tazila say God does not will evil, but Satan wills it and it occurs even when God does not will it, similar to the Zanadiqa claim that evil comes from Satan as a separate creator. Thus, Maturidi exposes the shared errors of these sects in denying God's complete power and will over all things, including evil.

Key Terms
القدرية
الخير
الشر
الإرادة
الشيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qadariyya and Mu'tazila are opposite sects with no common ground.
Correction: Maturidi shows that both, along with Zanadiqa, share the error of limiting God's power over evil.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Mu'tazila say about the will of evil?
A) God wills evil
B) Satan wills evil and it occurs
C) Evil does not exist
D) God creates evil

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that any denial of God's absolute power over good and evil compromises tawheed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God is in control of all things, including evil, how does that change the way you respond when you face injustice or suffering? Are you willing to trust God's wisdom even when you cannot see the good?
?
Consider the claim that Satan's will can override God's. Do you ever act as if Satan has more power in your life than God? What does this passage call you to examine about your own fears and reliance on God?
?
Maturidi shows that limiting God's power over evil leads to shirk. Can you identify any area in your life where you subconsciously attribute evil to something other than God's decree, and how might that affect your tawheed?

The Mu'tazila Position Leads to Attributing Error, Ignorance, and Incapability to God
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila via an analogy forcing error, ignorance, incapability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing that their view logically forces one to attribute error, ignorance, and incapability to God, using an analogy of two opponents.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's own reasoning traps them into the very defects they deny.

Imam Maturidi presents a powerful logical refutation of the Mu'tazila position on human action and divine will. He begins with a simple analogy of two opponents, then applies the same logic to show that the Mu'tazila inadvertently attribute error, ignorance, and weakness to God. This passage is a masterclass in dialectical argumentation (jadal).

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy of two opponents
Begin by reading Maturidi's description of two opponents whose actions go contrary to their intentions, each ending up in the other's power. This sets up the logical framework.
Notice how the analogy is presented as a concrete scenario.
2
Identify the three defects
From the analogy, Maturidi extracts three necessary consequences: error (khaṭa'), ignorance (jahl), and incapability ('ajz). Understand why each follows logically.
These three are central to the refutation.
3
Apply to the Mu'tazila view
Now see how Maturidi compares the Mu'tazila claims about God's intentions and empowerment. He shows that their view leads to the same three defects when God's creatures act contrary to His will.
The Mu'tazila say God only empowers for obedience, but disbelievers disobey – causing a mismatch.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the Mu'tazila position resembles the blameworthy analogy in every aspect, forcing them to attribute defects to God. Reflect on the strength of this reductio ad absurdum.
This is a classic kalam argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خرج فعلها على خلاف ما أرادا ، وصار كل واحد منهما في جهة من يد الآخر ، فلزمهم القول فى النور بالخطأ وبالجهل والعجز. أما الخطأ ، فلما لم يكن عاقبته على ما أراد ، والجهل ؛ لما لم يكن علم أنه يبقى في وثاق عدوه ، وأما العجز هو أنه في جهد الخلاص وتدبيره " ، فلم يتهيأ له . وكذلك قول المعتزلة : إن الله لم يقو كافرا ولا أحدا إلا ليطيعه ، ولا ملك أحدا شيئا إلا ليشكر ، ولا خلق [أحدا] إلا ليخضع له ، وكذلك؛ يريد ، وله فعل ما فعل ، ولو كان منه غير هذا كان يكون سفيها ظالما ، ثم لم يكن يجميع ما أعطى أعداءه ما أراد ، وله أخطاء ، وذلك الخطأ المعروف أن لا يخرج الأمر على ما يريده ، ثم القدرة على ما لم لو فعل لكان خارجا عن علمه ، ثم ثبت من الفعل فيما بعد هو فعل الله في المنع منه ، فأوجب قولهم مضاهاة من ذكرت بكل وجوه المذمة
His action [of the two opponents] came out contrary to what each intended, and each of them ended up in the hand of his enemy. Therefore, the statement about light necessarily leads to attributing error, ignorance, and incapability. As for error, because its consequence was not what he intended; ignorance, because he did not know that he would remain in the bonds of his enemy; and as for incapability, it is that he exerted effort for deliverance and planning but it was not achieved. Similarly, the statement of the Mu'tazila: that God does not empower a disbeliever or anyone except to obey Him, nor does He give anyone ownership of anything except to be grateful, nor does He create anyone except to submit to Him; likewise He wills, and He does what He does, and if it were otherwise from Him, He would be foolish and unjust. Then He did not achieve with all that He gave His enemies what He intended, so He has error; and that error is well-known: that the matter does not turn out as He wills. Then [as for] power over what He did not do—if He did it would be outside His knowledge—then it is established that the action thereafter is God's action in preventing it. So their statement necessitates resemblance to those I mentioned in every aspect of blame.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by argument. Maturidi begins with an analogy: two opponents each acting contrary to their plans, each ending up in the other's power. This forces attributing error, ignorance, and incapability to them. He then applies this to the Mu'tazila view: they claim God only empowers for obedience, gives ownership for gratitude, and creates for submission, and that God always wills and does accordingly. If an outcome were otherwise, they would call God foolish and unjust. Maturidi points out that in reality, God's enemies often get what they want contrary to God's supposed intention, which would mean God errs. Moreover, if God were unable to prevent an action, He would be incapable. Thus, the Mu'tazila position leads to the same blameworthy attributes they seek to avoid in their opponents.

Key Terms
الخطأ
الجهل
العجز
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi is endorsing anthropomorphism by attributing human flaws to God.
Correction: Maturidi is not attributing these to God; he is showing that the Mu'tazila position logically forces one to do so, which is absurd. His argument is a reductio ad absurdum.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what three defects does the Mu'tazila position force one to attribute to God?
A) Error, ignorance, and incapability
B) Injustice, foolishness, and weakness
C) Forgetfulness, helplessness, and malice
D) Lying, forgetfulness, and injustice

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's logical analogy shows that the Mu'tazila position inevitably forces one to attribute to God the very flaws of error, ignorance, and weakness they sought to avoid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own understanding of God's will and human actions, are you ever guilty of imposing human limitations on God while claiming to defend His transcendence? How can you ensure your reasoning does not lead to the same contradiction as the Mu'tazila?
?
The analogy in this passage shows that if our reasoning leads to attributing imperfection to God, we must reject that reasoning. Reflect on a belief you hold about God that might, if followed to its logical conclusion, imply something unworthy of Him. Are you willing to abandon that belief?
?
The Mu'tazila wanted to protect God from association with evil, but their position backfired. In your own life, are there areas where you try so hard to defend God's honor that you inadvertently diminish Him? How can you let God be God without forcing Him into your logical boxes?

Refuting Sects on Divine Action and Will
Maturidi refutes four sects on divine action and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes four deviant sects by showing their shared error of limiting God's absolute power and will.

Core Idea
All four sects diminish God's absolute sovereignty over creation and evil.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi exposes the logical parallels between seemingly different heretical groups. Though the Zandaqa, Mushabbiha, Mu'tazila, and Qadariyya appear to disagree, they all share a fundamental mistake: they place limits on God's power and will. By identifying their common flaw, Maturidi reaffirms the Sunni creed that God creates all actions and wills all that occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sects and their core claims
Read the passage and list each sect mentioned: Zandaqa, Mushabbiha, Mu'tazila, and Qadariyya. Note what each group denies or affirms about God's action and will.
Maturidi uses a concise style; each sect is introduced with 'وأنكرت' or 'وزعمت'.
2
Notice how Maturidi groups similar errors
Observe that Maturidi pairs Zandaqa with Mushabbiha on the issue of creation, and later compares Mu'tazila with Qadariyya on evil. This shows a pattern of shared assumptions.
The Zandaqa deny creation ex nihilo; Mushabbiha affirm a body – both limit God's absolute otherness.
3
Contrast the positions on human actions and evil
Mu'tazila deny that God creates human actions; Qadariyya claim God always does the utmost good and cannot do evil. Maturidi points out that both assign creation of evil to creatures.
For Mu'tazila, evil occurs because the devil wills it against God's will; for Qadariyya, evil is solely from humans.
4
Recognize the underlying Sunni principle
Maturidi's refutation implies the Sunni position: God creates all actions (good and evil) and wills everything that exists. No limit can be placed on His power or will.
This principle is not stated explicitly here but is the logical conclusion of his critique.
5
Reflect on the unity of heresies
Consider why Maturidi links these four groups. Despite their differences, all reduce God's sovereignty. The lesson is that any doctrine restricting God's power leads to deviation.
This reflects the Maturidi method of using reason to defend tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وأنكرت الزنادقة قول شيء يحدث لا من شيء؛ ما لا يتصوّر مثله فى الوهم، وكذلك المشبهة في قولهم بالجسم. وأنكرت المعتزلة خلق أفعال العباد؛ لما ليس بقائم في العقول ولا متوهم في الأوهام، وزعمت القدرية أن الله لا يدع الغاية من الخير الذي يقدر عليه إلا فعله. وكذلك قول الزنادقة أنه يفعل غاية الخير، وأن خالق الشر غيره. وكذلك قول القدرية أن الله لا يقدر على شيء موجود من الشر، وأنه كله فعل العباد. ويقول المعتزلة : إن الله لا يريد كون الشر لأحد، ويريده الشيطان، ثم يكون ذلك وإن لم يكن ما يريده الله، كما قالت الزنادقة في كون ذلك من الشيطان، وخالق الشر وإن لم يرده الله
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: The Zandaqa denied that anything comes into existence from nothing, [saying] it is not conceivable in imagination; similarly the Mushabbiha in their statement of corporeality. And the Mu'tazila denied the creation of the actions of servants, because it is not established in intellects nor imagined in fancies. And the Qadariyya claimed that God does not leave off the utmost good which He is able to do except that He does it. Similarly the statement of the Zandaqa that He does the utmost good, and that the creator of evil is other than Him. And similarly the statement of the Qadariyya that God is not able to do any existing evil, and that all of it is the act of servants. And the Mu'tazila say: God does not will the existence of evil for anyone, and the devil wills it, then it occurs even though it is not what God wills, just as the Zandaqa said concerning its occurrence from the devil, and the creator of evil even if God does not will it.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is a series of refutations. Maturidi lists four groups and their erroneous beliefs. The Zandaqa deny creation ex nihilo because they cannot imagine it; the Mushabbiha affirm anthropomorphism by saying God has a body. The Mu'tazila deny that God creates human actions because it is not rationally evident. The Qadariyya claim God always does the utmost good and cannot do evil. Maturidi then notes similarities: the Zandaqa say God does only good and evil is from another; the Qadariyya say God cannot produce evil, so evil comes from humans; the Mu'tazila say God does not will evil, but the devil wills it and it happens against God's will, paralleling the Zandaqa view that evil's creator is not God. The cumulative effect is to show that all these views diminish God's absolute power and sovereignty.

Key Terms
الزنادقة
المشبهة
المعتزلة
القدرية
خلق أفعال العباد
الشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Maturidi is merely reporting the views of these sects without refuting them.
Correction: Maturidi is implicitly refuting them by exposing their logical inconsistencies and shared error; his critique affirms the Sunni position by contrast.

Checkpoint
Which group did Maturidi say denies the creation of human actions because it is not rationally evident?
A) The Zandaqa
B) The Mushabbiha
C) The Mu'tazila
D) The Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that all these sects, despite differences, diminish God's absolute power and will, and the Sunni creed affirms that God creates all actions and wills all events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face evil or hardship, do you secretly wish God were not involved in it—like the Qadariyya who limit His power to protect His goodness? Will you instead affirm that He creates everything, including your trials, and submit to His wisdom even when you cannot see it?
?
You claim to believe God's will is absolute. But in your heart, do you sometimes think like the Mu'tazila—that God would never will something you consider evil? Are you willing to accept that His will encompasses all events, even those that trouble your conscience?
?
Maturidi shows that limiting God's power is a shared error among these sects. Where in your own life do you subtly limit God—by doubting He can bring good from your mistakes, or by refusing to see His hand in your suffering? Will you repent of such limits and trust His absolute sovereignty today?

The Objection Against Essential Attributes and Names
Maturidi reports an objection against essential attributes and names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection raised by some groups against essential attributes and names of Allah, and their reasoning that such language implies likeness to creatures.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's names due to fear of comparison leads to a false conclusion.

Imam Maturidi presents the view of a group who reject that Allah has essential attributes or names because they think it would imply similarity to created beings. They extend this reasoning to spatial descriptions. This objection sets the stage for the theological response that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's words set the context.
2
Identify the core argument
Look for why the group denies essential attributes and names. The key phrase is 'they thought that this necessitates likeness'.
Their reasoning: having a name like creatures implies tashbih.
3
Examine the extension to spatial language
Notice how they analogize from names to spatial descriptions (place). What conclusion do they draw about Allah and place?
They argue that spatial language would limit Allah, so they conclude either He is in every place or description by place is forbidden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : أنكر قوم أن يكون صفة الله ذاتية يوصف بها ، أو اسم ذاتي يعرف به ، وظنوا أن ذلك يوجب التشابه ؛ إذ له اسم كما كان لغيره ، وقالوا : وإذ لم يجز أن يكون له موافقة في شيء من جملة الخلق على الإشارة كان أدلة تحقيق الموافقة بالاسم الذي لكل شيء أحرى ؛ ولهذا أنكروا إليه القول بالشيء والعالم والقادر ، وضربوا له المثل – بأن القول له وفيه بالمكان ؛ إذ يوجب التشبيه والحد ، فهو بكل مكان ، كذلك إذ للأمكنة نهاية ، فالوصف بها وبالواحد منها واحد ، فمثله الأول ، وبالله التوفيق
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Some people denied that Allah has an essential attribute by which He is described, or an essential name by which He is known, and they thought that this necessitates likeness; because He has a name just as others have. And they said: Since it is not permissible for Him to have agreement with anything from the entirety of creation in terms of indication, then it is more appropriate that the proof of agreement by the name which everything has is more fitting; and for this reason they denied to Him the saying of 'thing', 'knower', and 'able', and they struck for Him a similitude – that the saying about Him and concerning Him of place necessitates comparison and limitation, so He is in every place, likewise, since places have an end, then description by them and by one of them is one, so His likeness is the first. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 692

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of a group (likely the Jahmiyya or Mu'tazila) who deny that Allah has essential attributes or names because they think this implies tashbih (likeness) to created beings. Their reasoning is: having a name like 'knower' or 'able' is something creatures also have, so it implies similarity. They extend this to spatial language, arguing that if Allah is described as being in a place, that would limit Him, so they conclude that He is in every place (or that description by place is forbidden). Maturidi reports their view without yet refuting it, setting up the need for a response. The phrase 'فمثله الأول' suggests that the first similitude is what they apply to Allah.

Key Terms
صفة ذاتية
اسم ذاتي
تشابه
تشبيه
وصف بالمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Having a name or attribute like 'knower' necessarily makes Allah similar to created beings.
Correction: Names and attributes are shared in meaning but not in essence. Allah's knowledge is unlike creation's; shared terminology does not imply shared reality.

Checkpoint
Why did the group mentioned in this passage deny that Allah has an essential attribute or name?
A) Because they thought it implies multiplicity in Allah.
B) Because they thought it implies likeness (tashbih) to creatures.
C) Because they found no textual evidence for names.
D) Because they held Allah is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
The objection against essential attributes is based on the mistaken assumption that shared names necessarily imply essential likeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call Allah 'The All-Knowing,' do you ever feel a tension because you also call a scholar 'knowing'? How does this lesson expose the risk of letting that tension lead you to downplay Allah's attributes? What will you do to affirm His names without hesitation?
?
Have you ever avoided reflecting deeply on a name of Allah because it felt too abstract or uncomfortable? What does this lesson say about the danger of such avoidance? Are you willing to study the names more deeply, trusting that they are true even if your mind cannot fully grasp them?
?
The objectors in this lesson struck a simile to justify their denial. What similes or analogies do you unconsciously use to try to understand Allah? How might those be misleading, and what is the corrective?

The Prophetic Proof: Names Do Not Imply Likeness
Maturidi argues that the prophets' use of names proves they do not imply tashbih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the example of the prophets to prove that divine names do not imply anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Core Idea
Prophets could not have brought names implying likeness, for that would break tawhid.

Imam Maturidi presents a compelling argument from the practice of the prophets themselves. Since all prophets called people to the oneness of Allah, if the names they used implied similarity to creation, they would be undermining the very message they came to deliver. This passage shows why such an implication is impossible and how the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him' safeguards transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument settle in your mind.
Notice the key phrase 'لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ' which appears at the end.
2
Identify the logical structure
Break the argument into two parts: (1) the proof from the prophets' mission, (2) the role of the Quranic verse in negating similarity. See how each part supports the conclusion.
Maturidi uses a conditional: 'if...then...' to show the impossibility of tashbih.
3
Reflect on the types of things negated
Note that the verse negates 'thingness' from simple perceptions (accidents and attributes) and composite entities (bodies). This shows that no created category resembles Allah.
This is a comprehensive negation that includes both attributes and physical forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على ما قلنا مجيء الرسل والكتب السماوية بها، ولو كان في التسمية بما جاءت به الرسل تشبيه لكانوا سبب نقض التوحيد، وهم جميعا دعوا إلى عبادة الواحد وإلى معرفة وحدانية الباري، لم يجز أن يكون ذلك مما يحقق العدد ويثبت الموافقة للخلق، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولكن لما احتملت تلك الأسماء خروج المسمى بها عن المعروفين من المسمين بها جاز مجيئهم بها مع قوله: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ لينفي به شيئية الأشياء من الإدراكات البسيطة وهي الأعراض والصفات والأعيان المركبة وهي الأجسام، وبالله المعونة.
Then the proof for what we have said is the coming of the messengers and the heavenly books with them. And if there were, in the naming by what the messengers brought, any likeness, they would be a cause of breaking tawhid, while they all called to the worship of the One and to the knowledge of the oneness of the Creator. It is not possible that this should be something that establishes multiplicity and affirms agreement with creation. And there is no power except through Allah. But since those names admit the possibility that the named one transcends those who are known among the named ones, it is permissible for them to come with them, along with His saying: 'There is nothing like Him' (42:11) to negate by it the 'thingness' of things from simple perceptions – which are accidents and attributes – and composite entities – which are bodies. And with Allah is assistance.
Source pages p. 693

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the practice of prophets. Maturidi argues that the prophets and scriptures came with these names (e.g., Knower, Able). If these names implied tashbih, then the prophets would be undermining tawhid, whereas they actually call to the worship of the One. Therefore, the names cannot imply likeness. Moreover, the names can be used because they allow the named (Allah) to transcend the usual referents (creatures). The verse 'laysa kamithlihi shay' (There is nothing like Him) is cited to negate any similarity, including from simple perceptions (accidents and attributes) and composite entities (bodies). So the names are safe because they come with this negation.

Key Terms
الرسل
الكتب السماوية
نقض التوحيد
لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ
الإدراكات البسيطة
الأعراض
الصفات
الأعيان المركبة
الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that using names like 'Knower' for God necessarily likens Him to human knowers, implying anthropomorphism.
Correction: Maturidi shows that prophets used these names while calling to tawhid, so they cannot imply likeness. The verse 'There is nothing like Him' affirms that the meanings are transcendent.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi use the example of the prophets to counter the objection that names imply tashbih?
A) He says prophets used names but only for unlettered people.
B) He argues that if names implied tashbih, prophets would be breaking tawhid, which they cannot do.
C) He claims prophets used only the name 'Allah'.
D) He says the names were changed after the prophets.

Key Takeaway
The prophets' unanimous call to tawhid proves that the names they used cannot imply likeness to creation, and the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him' reinforces this by negating all similarity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is Merciful', do you ever imagine a human-like mercy? How can you train your heart to affirm the name while negating all similarity?
?
The prophets called to tawhid without falling into tashbih. In your own speech about God, what words or images do you need to purify to avoid inadvertently implying likeness?
?
You recite 'There is nothing like Him' regularly. But does that verse actually govern how you think about every attribute of God? If it did, what would you have to change about your inner picture of Him starting today?

4 min
The Batiniyya's Diversion of Divine Names
Maturidi mentions the Batiniyya who interpret names as referring to an emanationist first principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Batiniyya esoterically reinterpret the divine names as emanationist principles and how Maturidi implicitly refutes this by exposing their allegorical method.

Core Idea
The Batiniyya turn the names of Allah into a Neoplatonic ladder of intellect and soul.

Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid is not only a defense of orthodox theology but also a refutation of deviant sects. In this brief passage, he mentions the Batiniyya (esotericists) who twist the divine names mentioned earlier to refer to a first originator and a second intellect and soul. By exposing their allegorical method, Maturidi warns against any reinterpretation that strips the names of their direct reference to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: الباطنية, المبدع الأول, الثاني, العقل, النفس.
This passage is very concise; every word carries weight.
2
Identify their core claim
The Batiniyya 'divert the mentioned names to the first originator and the second'. Ask yourself: what are these 'mentioned names'? They are the divine names discussed earlier in the text.
They reinterpret names like 'First', 'Creator' as referring to emanated principles.
3
Recognize the philosophical influence
The 'first' and 'second' likely refer to the Neoplatonic First Intellect (al-aql) and Soul (al-nafs). The Batiniyya adopted this emanationist cosmology.
This is a foreign philosophical intrusion into Islamic theology.
4
Understand Maturidi's implied rejection
Maturidi does not explicitly rebut here, but by reporting their view in a work of orthodox theology, he implicitly condemns it. The reader is expected to see that divine names cannot be diverted to created entities.
Maturidi's method is to expose and let the absurdity speak for itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت الباطنية وهم الذين يصرفون المذكور من الأسماء إلى المبدع الأول والثاني نمو العقل والنفس، ويجعلون كل العالم مبروزا في العقل تستمد منه النفس
And the Batiniyya said – and they are those who divert the mentioned names to the first originator and the second, the growth of the intellect and the soul, and they make the whole world manifested in the intellect from which the soul derives sustenance.
Source pages p. 693

Commentary
This passage briefly identifies a heretical group, the Batiniyya (esotericists), who reinterpret the divine names (mentioned earlier) as referring not to Allah but to a first principle (al-mubdi' al-awwal) and a second principle (perhaps the First Intellect and Soul in Neoplatonic emanation). They view the entire world as appearing in the intellect, with the soul deriving from it. This is a concise condemnation of their allegorical tampering with the names, which Maturidi rejects by implication.

Key Terms
الباطنية
المبدع الأول
الثاني
العقل
النفس

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what do the Batiniyya do with the divine names?
A) They deny them completely.
B) They divert them to a first originator and a second (intellect and soul).
C) They add more names.
D) They use only the name 'Allah'.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya's allegorical reinterpretation of divine names as referring to a first intellect and soul is a distortion that Maturidi implicitly rejects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been tempted to think of Allah's attributes, like His being 'First', as referring to some abstract principle rather than directly to Him? How does this lesson expose that as a subtle form of distancing yourself from the living God? What will you do to guard against that today?
?
If the Batiniyya could take the beautiful names of Allah and reassign them to created intellects, what names of Allah have you unconsciously disconnected from your daily life? Will you recommit to addressing Allah by those names directly, with full conviction that He alone is their source?
