Further Materialist Views: Four Natures and Single Nature
Maturidi presents two further materialist views and critiques the argument for a Maker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two additional materialist positions: one that makes the four natures the origin but with substances having their own origin, and another that posits a single nature as the cause of the world, leading to a flawed argument for a Maker.

Core Idea
Materialists who affirm a Maker still end up with contradictions.

After presenting the first materialist group, Imam al-Maturidi describes two more nuanced positions. One group views the four natures as the origin but considers natures incidental to substances. Another group posits a single nature that necessitates the world's eternity, yet they attempt to prove the existence of a Maker through the coherence of creation. Maturidi points out the inconsistency in their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic sub-passage covering both groups. Note the transition from 'وَمِنْهُمْ' (and among them).
2
Identify the two groups
The first subgroup says the origin is the four natures but each substance has its own origin. The second says there is one nature that causes the world.
3
Understand the argument for a Maker
The second group uses the coherence and perfection of things to prove a knowing Manager, because nature lacks power.
They affirm a Maker.
4
Spot the flaw
They then claim the world is eternal, which contradicts the idea of a powerful Creator whose power would necessitate creation. The author ends with 'There is no power except with God.'
This is the critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنهم اختلفوا : فمنهم من يجعله كذلك على ما بينا ، من غير أن يكون له صنع وعلى هذا يخرج مذهب أصحاب الطبائع : إن التفاوت والاختلاف على اختلاف الطبائع وتفاصيلها ، وسماها قوم هيولى ، والتفاوت فى الذي ذكرت على مثال الأصباغ : إنها تخرج على ألوان مختلفة بتفاوت المزاج واعتداله ، وعلى ذلك جعلوا جوهر البشر من اعتدال الطبائع ، والدواب من اضطرابه ، وعلى هذا كل شيء . ومنهم من يرى أصله الأربع من الطبائع ، ولكن لكل جوهر أصلا ، والطبائع دخيلة فيها. ومنهم من جعله كذلك بالطبائع ويقول : هو واحد ، ويجعله علة تكون العالم ، فيوجب قدمه بوجوده ، ويذهب في اثبات الصانع إلى اتساق الأشياء واتقانها ؛ إذ ذلك لا يكون إلا بمدير عليم ، إذ الطبع لا يرجع إلى قدرة ، و به صلاح الأشياء ، فقالوا بالصانع ، ثم إذ هو كان في الأزل فأوجبوا كون العالم فى الأزل على نحو اقتران الأشياء بعلاها ، على أنه إذ كان العالم مواهبه و تعميه و تبعمه ، وأنه قادر بذاته فثبت وجوده وكرمه بذاته ، فيلزم كون الذي كرمه يوجبه ، وقدرته توجده ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
But they differed: some of them made it as we described, without any act of creation, and upon this goes the school of the adherents of natures (taba'i'): that difference and diversity are according to the diversity of natures and their details, and some people called them matter (hayula). The diversity in what I mentioned is like the example of dyes: they come out in different colors due to the difference and balance of the mixture. Upon that, they considered the substance of humans from the balance of natures, and of beasts from their imbalance, and upon this everything. And among them is one who thinks its origin is the four natures, but each substance has an origin, and the natures are incidental in them. And among them is one who made it likewise by natures and says: it is one, and he makes it the cause of the world's coming-to-be, thereby necessitating its eternity by its existence. He goes in proving the Maker to the coherence and perfection of things, for that cannot be except by a knowing Manager, for nature does not refer to power, and through Him is the good order of things. So they affirmed the Maker. Then when He was eternal, they necessitated the world's coming-to-be in eternity in the manner of the connection of things with their causes, upon that when the world was [??], and that He is powerful by His essence, so His existence and generosity are established by His essence. Therefore, it follows that what He has bestowed necessitates it, and His power brings it into existence. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 711

Commentary
This passage classifies and describes various materialist views about the origin of the world. The author, Imam al-Maturidi, begins by noting that those who reject divine action in the world still differ among themselves. The first group described are those who attribute all diversity to the four natures (taba'i') and their combinations, comparing them to dyes that produce different colors based on mixture. They believe that human essence is from a balance of natures, while animals are from imbalance. Then he mentions a subgroup that considers the four natures as origins but each substance has its own origin with natures being incidental. Another group posits a single nature as the cause of the world, necessitating the world's eternity, and then tries to prove the Maker through the coherence and perfection of things, arguing that nature does not have power. They end up affirming a Maker but then claim the world is eternal, which leads to a contradiction: if the Maker is powerful by essence, then His power would necessitate the world's existence eternally. The author concludes this section with the statement 'There is no power except with God', indicating the insufficiency of such views.

Key Terms
طبائع (taba'i')
أربع (four)
صانع (Maker)
قدرة (power)
أزل (eternity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all materialists deny a Creator completely.
Correction: The second subgroup actually affirms a Maker, but their argument leads to an eternal world, which is problematic.

Checkpoint
What is the key reason the second subgroup gives for proving a Maker?
A) The existence of evil
B) The coherence and perfection of things
C) The diversity of natures
D) The need for a first cause

Key Takeaway
The materialists' attempt to combine a single nature with a Maker leads to the problematic conclusion that the world is eternal alongside God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the intricate order of the universe, does it ever feel easier to believe it always existed rather than submit to a Creator who brought it into being from nothing? What part of you resists that submission?
?
The materialists in this lesson used the same evidence of design that you might use to argue for God, yet they ended up with a world that is eternal and independent. How can you ensure that your reasoning about God does not lead you to compromise the truth of His absolute power and freedom?
?
If you truly believed that God's power is not bound by any necessity—not even the necessity of an eternal universe—how would that change the way you think about your own life, your struggles, and the times when you feel trapped by circumstances? What would it look like to live in that freedom today?
